However, the solution to be presented acts more specifically at environment-level rather than per program-basis, please keep that in mind.\r\n\r\nEssentially, on the machines requesting connections to the server, with \"Administrator privileges\" at hand (and assuming those machines runs with OS Windows), handle the following:\r\n* Open the **command prompt**. For that: click Start menu, search \"cmd\", then press Enter;\r\n* Type \"`netsh int ipv4 set dynamicport tcp start=<base_port_id> num=<pool_limit>`\", pool_limit: 255+;\r\n* Open the game.\r\n\r\nAssuming all procedures went fine, IoSessions should get pinged within the given range. This should be an action to be implemented on each machine running the game.\r\n\r\nMore info on [https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/929851/the-default-dynamic-port-range-for-tcp-ip-has-changed-in-windows-vista](https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/help/929851/the-default-dynamic-port-range-for-tcp-ip-has-changed-in-windows-vista)\r\n\r\nGood entertainment for your class.\r\n\r\nBest regards,\r\nRonan"}}, "public": true, "created_at": "2019-11-13T02:51:57Z"}, {"id": "10774338267", "type": "IssueCommentEvent", "actor": {"id": 9257761, To do it, `MapleQuest::reset(MapleCharacter chr)` covers the situation, as it flags a given `MapleQuest.getInstance(int questid)` as NOT_STARTED.\r\n\r\nTherefore, you should iterate over all quests the player currently holds.
